--- 帖子 #1 ---
Hello traders,

I recently found out chaos system and read the books about it (by Bill Williams). I was convinced by the reading I tried the system for a while...

I seems worthable for me and I didn't find discussions here about this trading system and here it is:

Profitunity System

On the chart apply following tools
Alligator - Three SMAs (13/8/5) with a future offset of 8/5/3 respactively.
Fractals  - 5 bars sequence where middle one has highest High / lowest Low and its preceded and followed two bars have lower highs / higher lows

preceded by two lower highs and is followed by two lower highs
Awesome Oscillator (AO) - difference between the 34-period and 5-period simple moving averages of the bar's midpoints (H+L)/2
Acceleration Oscillator (AC) - difference between 5/34 momentum histogram (AO) and a 5-bar simple moving average on the AO

To apply then into MetaTrader 4 platform use these menus
Alligator:  Insert -> Indicators -> Bill Williams –> Alligator
Fractals:   Insert -> Indicators -> Bill Williams –> Fractals
Awesome Oscillator: Insert -> Indicators -> Bill Williams –> Awesome Oscillator
Acceleration Oscillator: Insert -> Indicators -> Bill Williams –> Acceleration Oscillator

Entry:

When (Alligator) lines are opening we put a buy stop one point above the most recent fractal outside of the lines in trend direction

Exit:

When (Alligator) lines are closing we are closing too.

we stay out of the market when and while lines are intertwining.

Adding:

After the first fractal is taken, we take any and every signal in that direction.

Adding Entry Signals:
AO: we go long when AO cross zero line from negative to positive values and short on the opposite scenario. we go long we have 3 consecutive AO bars above zero line last two having higher highs (i.e. AO pulls back for a while) - opposite for sell

AC:Go long after two consecutive bars above zero line Go long after three consecutive bars below zero line - for short - reverse scenario

________________________________________________________________

That's it. If you need more info - you could read more here

I'll try to answer any questions as best as I can...

--- 帖子 #8 ---
There is another tool that could be useful

Gator: in MT use menu Insert -> Indicators -> Bill Williams –> Gator

It measues the distance between MA (Alligator) lines. It is useful because it shows you at a glance whether MAs are opening, closing or intertwining.

Trade after it becomes green.

Here is a sample&

when Gator is green - it is time to look around, but while there is not a fractal taken in this direction we do not enter the market

when Gator is red - it is time to take profit and/or wait for the next chance

Hope it will be useful to your trading

!i!

--- 帖子 #18 ---
Hi james275,

I've tried to describe signals in my 1st post here.

Here under I'll try to summarize them in brief...:

There are 5 tools issuing signals:

One enter the market when 1st fractal (#1) out of the lines is hit again.

Once on the market one opens a new order is same direction when any of the other signals is triggered.

These are: AO(#2), AC(#3), Zone(#4) and Balance Line(#5).

Some of them issue more than one signal.

If more than one signal is triggered simultaneously - corresponding number of orders are opened.

I personaly am taking each of the signal until my money management rules allow this.

I've tried to comment the charts attached in previous posts, pointing where signals are and where stops are.

If you have any questions please let me know - I'll do my best to answer them.

!i!

BTW - this method is described in "New Trading Dimensions" book by Bill Williams.

There is slight alterations of the system in his next book "Trading Chaos" 2nd edition

--- 帖子 #24 ---
I looked into this briefly. I believe it was intended for daily timeframes originally and meant to take in trending sections (Alligator opens it's mouth etc).

Imho back when I checked it simply lagged price lightyears due to relying on so god awful many moving averages/oscillators and caught the last 5-15% of most moves if at all.

Did not convince me at all. Even most 4h EMA crosses would most likely do better on average(especially with pullback entries).

If you can make it work for you, all the better, but imho it's just making a basic concept (if the market moves strongly, follow it) a lot more complicated than it needs to be. Even a Breakout system is a lot more effective.

Ask our good friend MrTrend or have a look at StevieT....super simple approach, still gets net pips.

Just my opinion.

Take care,

SeekingLight

--- 帖子 #26 ---
Hello

I've re-read the last book about Chaos by BW and decided to add the rule about "Reverse bar".

It is quite simple one and if succed could final with a good profit, if not, the loss will be reduced (I hope)

So here are the rules:

Bearish Reversla Bar - sell orders

1. Bar with higher high that closes in the botom half - that should mean that bulls have been stronger at the beginning but next bears have superiority at bar closing.

2. Prices must be far away from the lines and must have obvious angle increase (opening) between MA lines and line drawn on the lows.

Entry:

Sell stop close below the low of the reverse bar

Stop loss little above the high of the same bar

That's it. Reverse for buy (use highs not lows!)

Why this is added? - If succeed it will allow an earlier entry.

--- 帖子 #44 ---
Hello Jim

Until Larry answer the questions, here is Bill Williams point of view as it is layed in his books (in brief trnasformed by myself):

In past years trends have been strong and relatively long this is why he suggests to add a contract on each signal. Nowadays trends are less long and are rare and this is why we have to profit from short moves increasing contracts on each signal. He also suggest adding in following proportion:

1:5:4:3:2 - i.e. 1st signal 1 contract; 2nd - 5 contracts; 3rd - 4 contracts and so on...

I personally do not use the above system, but dicide on each signal depending on overall situation of the market....

Regards...

--- 帖子 #56 ---
Jim No:

I apologize for the tardy response... I've been off playing grandpa.

First, my position sizing and risk management rules tell me exactly my lot limit for a trade; and for me "a trade" begins when I get on board a directional move and includes any subsequent add-on lots. A trade is opened only on a signal from one of the Three Wise Men. Here is how I normally allocate that lot limit:By my rule, I commit only 1 lot per buy/sell signal. Once a trade is opened, a signal is valid only if its fill will be beyond the Alligator in the direction of the trade. As long as my trade is profitable, I take all valid Profitunity trade signals until my lot limit is reached or the trade is closed. Valid Profitunity trade signals include those described in Bill Williams' second book, New Trading Dimensions. Before adding on to a profitable position, pay strict attention to how the add-on will impact trade risk limits and where breakeven is!

...\larry.bye

--- 帖子 #63 ---
I have been trading the spot Forex almost exclusively since I discovered it in 2004; but prior to that, I traded the futures markets.  I was introduced to the Profitunity methodology and strategies in late 1998 or early 1999 as I recall.  As a futures trader, I used only EOD data and traded off daily charts; and I traded the Profitunity way pretty much as it was spelled out in Bill Williams' second book, New Trading Dimensions.  The only time I use its "pile it on" approach in my Forex trading is when I have been lucky enough to catch a new daily chart trend that reversed after getting hit by the "5 magic bullets" that ended the previous trend.  I am mostly an intraday trader now, but there still is a lot of Profitunity in how I now trade.  Yes, Profitunity has been very good to me.  I personally think that to use all of its entry signals and exit strategies, one needs to be trading it in the daily time frame.

...\larry.bye

--- 帖子 #65 ---
Here is something that may interest some of you re the 1st and 2nd Wise Men that were introduced in Trading Chaos, 2nd Edition.  They may be more useful as filters than entry signals.  One of my trading strategies for the M5 time frame is to nest a buy order above the VFH when the AO bar is green, and to nest a sell order below the VFL when the AO bar is red... whether or not the AO bar is positive or negative.  Could more pips be captured if I required any entry signals generated by the 1st or 2nd Wise Men to have been hit before nesting a 3rd Wise Man order?  In other words, would a signal failure by the 1st or 2nd Wise Men keep me out of more loss or low profit trades?  I started looking at this because I am reluctant to enter a trade on the wrong side of the Alligator... most of us old-time Profitunity disciples likely are having trouble with that!

...\larry.bye

--- 帖子 #68 ---
Hello Larry,

Thank you for sharing the above with us.

I'd like to add that the Chaos Trading System is designed basically for tranding markets rather than sideway moves and adding is very useful when a trand is on.

In the book, you've mentioned, is noted than trands are more and more rare. This is why a new approach is required.

It is Divergent Bar - an attempt to enter market on the least sign of trend reversal. As one could guess - this increase potential profit, if trend reverse. Increasing potential profit corresponds with increased risk. This brings into the world new, so called, pink [purple] line.

Pink line is 5 SMA shifted 3 bars to the right. It is serving as a stop loss - trade have to be closed when there are two bars closing on the opposite of the movement side.

Finally: nevertheless which side one enters the market there is an ever lasting dilemma:If we enter the market using DBar - the signal might turn to a false one If we don't - we might miss a substantial move and market to turn around just after taking the fractal. Last two trades (post #66 & post #67) are good samples of the above.

Perhaps this is why a substantial part of the book is devoted to trader's mind...

--- 帖子 #94 ---
Hello Miguel

There are two things I look for:Stable move in one direction Greater angle between price and red line (Alligator's teeth)

As you could see on the chart - neither of the mentioned exists - move has been killed by double bottom; there is almost lack of angle

The probabbility movement to reverse to down direction after double bottom is relatively small. Support to this is idea give weekly and monthly charts where double bottom also apear. Prices need some force and time to mustering it.

Acctually if you have taken the 1st DBar you could collect some profit...

I personally prefer to trade only when I have clear picture about the situation and stay out if I have any hesitations.

Even now up move could break (i.e. on the news) and reverse...

No one knows ... but everyone must be prepared and to have clear plan what to do in either case...

You also could reffer to post #26 for more info about DBar.

--- 帖子 #107 ---
Hello Miguel

I'm glad you like this system.

Francly speaking I also had dificulties (this is for every begining, eh?) when I started. Even now I make lots of mistakes

Clear though the system require very titgh rule following because the trader easely could decide that current movement is accidental and soon will tun in "our direction".

As you could see from the previous post I am also often surprised by the market direction. There is no tool capable to predict market direction, especially forex. Probabilities - yes, but prediction... Last trade (post #104) was a (pleasent for me) surprise and the only reason I was in and made profit was following the rules.

DBar rules are simple. DBar has preceeding:steep move acute angle buy/sell stop order above/below the DBar

Next is patiance (easy to say ; hard to follow  ) and always keep an eye on the stops.

Another sample I would point is this post #105 where it could seems the exit earlier but by my rules.

But this depends on one style of trading.

I personally prefer to lock profit when I've any doubt - actual profit is better than actual loss based on a hypothetical begger profit  .

If you have questions I'll try to answer them. Read the books though. They are good and comprihensive.

Hallo Invincible

These, you see on the charts, are just the same signals I've described but because I do lots of things concurrently I need some alerts to draw my attention to the chart.

I do not beleve to "black box" things telling me when and how much to enter or exit the market. This leeds to loss only. If you do  not understand what are you doing even the best indicator or expert won't help you make profit.

So I sit on my ... chair and scribbled an indicator

I also used to hunt tools previously to beat the market with, but the market proved  (painfully for  ) me that the best tool is my mind - no one else could help me.

I'll quote by hart B.Williams - "We trade our believes"

This is why I did not offer this indicator up to know.

Another reason is that all this is still under development. There are some thing to be mastered. When ready (hope soon) and if results are satisfying I'll consider some sort of distribution if there is any interest of it.

For the moment I'm not ready to do this because (you could see around) there are lot's of complains, improvement suggestions and so on which I cannot neither answer nor deal with.

Finally - writing of an indicator is not hard - creating the system is....

Here is an attempt to explain fractal.

Bars 1 through 5 are creating fractal on bar 3 which has higher high than the preceeding two bars (1 & 2), right?

Bars 4 and 5 have lower highs that bar 3 and this is the condition - at least 5 bars where we have a bar with a higher high than the others and we have two lower highs on both side of fractal bar - this is for bullish fractal.

So on the drawing below you have a bulish fractal on bar 3, right?

let say the high price is 1.2345 so you entry point is 1 tick above, i.e. you put buy stop order on 1.2346.

Actual long side entry is on bar 8 because bars between 3 and 8 have lower high than fractal bar (#3) and bar 8 has reach a price higher than our fractal (1.2345).

Hope I've written all this clear enough

'Fractals are valid until they are either triggered or a new fractal in the same direction appears ...'

In other words - a new fractal IN THE SAME DIRECTION invalidates the previous fractal and associated order IN THE SAME DIRECTION!

That could work!

The only problem I forsee here is if you brokerr is one of those that hunts stops (which mine regularly does). If you have that problem I would err on the side of caution and place your orders above the fractal itself NOT above the high of the candlestick or bar where the fractal is attached. That way your orders would only be executed when a genuine move occurs and not when 'spiked'. You would be getting into a trade a bit later BUT at least you would have ammunition with which to approach your broker to exact a refund!

Hello Dale

Sorry for this delay but I've problem with my PCs

This is the answer of post #167.

My experience shows me that the lower time frame is the most dificult to manage trades - but this is only my oppinion.

to your chart - general rule is: we take only sell signals that atr below the alligator and buy signals only above alligator.

Because we are below the lines we look only for sell signals.

Black arrows mark sell fractals - below we place sell stop orders;

Green lines are actual entry point in the market - where sell stop orders (placed below the fractals) has been executed.

That's it

--- 帖子 #173 ---
This does not make sense.

Fractals in same direction confirm the signal  rather than to invalidate it.

We use it to add orders in trend direction.We get first fractal outside of the Alligator and enter market on the trend direction. We add on each consecutive signal after the 1st fractal is taken - i.e. price has moved above/below fractal's high/low

how much above high or below low of the candle you'll put the order is a personal decision. You could use stop orders or you could do it manually.

If this is a trend beginning there is no problem to enter late, but this won't keep you dry  from 'spikes'...

Yes

Sorry - I should have been more clear:

What I meant was that this applies ONLY when opening a position.  Only after the position is open / order has been triggered do you use the subsequent fractals in the same direction to add to the position BUT when opening the position only the last fractal in an up or down position is valid i.e. a new fractal in the same direction invalidates the previous fractal and order in the same direction (of course all of this taking the Alligator into account).

I'm a big fan of Parabolic SAR and (as you probably know) this indicator was specifically designed to agressively protect profits / negate losses so today I will experiment by placing my stop loss on orders at the CURRENT value of Parabolic SAR and keep adjusting the stop loss as new dots appear i.e. as if you were already in a trade. I do not take so strict the words.

The general idea behind chaos trading system is to trade with trend and to stay in as long as possible.

Signals are only to make things clear for the trader and to asure that trader will enter on the right side of the market.

Fractals, as a signal, are place where direction changes. So once formed thay say one only thing - 'here is an edge', i.e. direction has changed. Once created it is always valid. It is only a mark.

Trades are made by us and to quote the book "we trade our believes".

--- 帖子 #184 ---
Hi sierra,

well stop positioning is another complicated stuff - it depensds on lot's of factors...

I use few diffenet stop loss placing rules. Generaly I put them away so as to avoid accident hits. I use them as a last firewall, i.e. I prefer to exit trades manually if they do not develop as expected.

One of the main point to detemine stoploss is the pair itself - it is useless to set same stop loss (i.e. 5, 50, 150 pips) on EURUSD and EURAUD for exapmle (this is only my point of view of caurse)

Another one is the picture from upper time trames - I use one type of stop loss at the beginning of the move, another after trend is clear enough and still another when Allicator starts closing its mouth...

In one word - I stop loss placement depends on the current market picture.

Hello everyone (and isto),

isto - you asked if anyone had any input with regard to false signals.

Well - here is my trillion dollars worth:

I started using this system last Monday (after I had had a hard time trying to understand the fractal signals) and I can honestly say that apart from the first day (last Monday) that I started using this system I have made consistent net profit every single day since using this system.

Like I said before - I am a firm believer in anything Bill Williams and J. Welles Wilder but I could never get my head around the fractal thing until last week (thanks to incorrect information in my charts manual - and yes - isto - the charts manual that I have is indeed incorrect - but that's of no consequence now anyway)!

Anyway - as far as false fractal signals are concerned - I have had a look at the weekly and daily charts of the instruments that I normally trade i.e. DAX 30, Dow, Nasdaq 100, S&P 500, MSCI Taiwan, Hang Seng Index, Nikkei 225, Gold, Silver, Crude Oil, and the SP500 (ASX) and I have found that yes there may be false signals EVEN when buying above the alligators lips or selling below the alligators jaw BUT the profitable trades BY FAR outweigh the losing trades AS LONG AS YOU USE STOPS - and that is the key here. In my opinion this is the 'Holy Grail' of trading systems (at least for me) BUT money management will make or break this system.

So far - I have followed the system 'to the letter' - but with the instruments that I trade - it appears that if I 'break the rules' just slightly i.e. buying or selling as soon as a buy or sell fractal appears close to the alligator's teeth (and not necessarily when the fractals appear on the right side of the teeth either) profits are maximized even with small losses.

As a matter of fact - on long term trades - I reckon you could get away without the alligator i.e. open an order for all and every single fractal that appears (obviously removing the previous order when a new fractal appears) although I know that this is diverging from the overall purpose and theme of this system i.e. to keep you in a trend and stay in for as long as possible.

I have attached a graph to demonstrate what I mean (it is the weekly chart for the DAX 30).

You'll note that I have taken the fractal signals regardless of whether or not they are on the right side of the teeth i.e. as long as they are close to the teeth no problem.

The DAX 30 is probably a bad example to demonstrate false signals because it trends most of the time but even in a ranging market this system works for the simple reason that unless there is a breakout from the range you are not actually in the market until the breakout happens so although you may have to wait some time for this happen when it does you're good to go.

I find my biggest problem with this system is when to take profit i.e. although I am doing fantastic with this system I tend to take profit far too early and Mr Williams does not seem to cover this too well although if the truth be told I am still developing trust in the system and I reckon once you have developed this trust and confidence and are prepared to see the trade through to its end based on the alligator then everything is good!

Regards,

Dale.

--- 帖子 #191 ---
The AO can be of some help here. Require the bar color to be supportive of the direction before nesting an entry order off of a fractal signal. Remember that a flat look of the extended Alligator balance lines is Bill's preferred entry setup. He is not concerned whether the signal is true or false; that's why he called this setup a "low rent district." Remember too, a fractal cannot give a valid signal unless it is 1) the most recent fractal in that direction and 2) a hit on it would be above the Alligator's teeth if buying; below them if selling.  Requiring that hit to also be above all Alligator balance lines makes a lot of sense to me; certainly when looking at Bill's preferred entry setup.

Hello,

OK - I have attached another chart as requested - with details as to where I would have placed my orders and stop loss.

The only problem with this system (is it a problem - I don't know) is that you can wait for a long long time to get the signals BUT when you do get them you are pretty much in the money BIG TIME!

Because I only started using this system last week I have not received a valid weekly or daily signal as yet and this is where the money is!

I have made on the four hour charts every day though but nothing like what is possible on the daily and weekly charts - can't wait for one of these signals my man!

I cannot demonstrate to you where I take profit purely because I don't know myself yet! Put it this way - on a $50 lot I have been happy to close the position when it has made a $100 - $200 profit BUT every single time I have done this the price has continued to move and in some instances the same lot could have been $1000 profit or more - and that kills me! Like I said - I just have to develop more faith in the system (myself with the system?) so that I can leave the positions open until maturity and this is hard to do!

By the way - I have tried this on 1 minute and 5 minute and 15 minute charts but I have lost pretty much most of the time so for anybody wanting to use this system I don't advocate using it on short time frames - I reckon 4 hours minimum and 1 day and 1 week preferred - on the longer time frames there is less chance (if any) of the trade going against you and the profits are MUCH bigger for much less risk. The only problem with this though is that your stop loss can be HUGE and it takes strength of character to not close out the position because you are getting edgy because the trade appears to be going against you. What is working for me so far (on the 4 hour charts) is: open the position, set the stop loss, and NEVER make it bigger and NEVER close the position UNLESS you want to take profit i.e. do not touch the position until you either take profit or the stop loss is hit. What I do is every hour or so refresh my chart and then move the stop loss closer to the price (I think I mentioned that I use the alligator's lips as the stop loss as per Bill) as per the value of the alligators lips. I am also a great fan of Parabolic SAR so I have this on all of my charts as well and I tend to compare the value of Parabolic SAR and the alligator's lips and use the lesser of the two BUT this depends on what the movements are like in the market i.e. volatile - I use the alligators lips otherwise Parabolic SAR ALTHOUGH this is not ideal because there have been times when the stop set with Parabolic SAR has been hit but the stop that would have been set using the alligator's lips would not have been hit and the position then continued to make profit. Fortuanately even although the stop set using the Parabolic SAR figure is hit the position the position is normally in a profit situation by this stage so profit is taken although it is of course less.

Let's keep this thread going - this system REALLY works (as a matter of fact I read somewhere the other day that it ranks as one of the all time best or 'classic' trading systems - I just can't remember where I saw it but if I find it I'll post the article).

I have not yet plucked up the courage to add to positions as new signals appear in the same (right) direction - don't ask me why - I'm chicken - but again - it will come!

I have tried this system on currency pairs but strangely enough have not made too much but I think it's because of the PIP values - too low for my liking - you are laying out $50 to make maybe $5 - not good risk/reward ration in my opinion - not anymore for me anyway. As a matter of fact only the DAX and the MSCI Taiwan are worth the trouble - even the Dow, S&P, etc. etc. are too little payback. Gold and Silver - also good.

I think the REAL merit of this system is the fact that it does not take market sentiment or any other nonsense into account - that's why it works. The only place where this comes into play is if you use the MFI and even that is technical really not so?

--- 帖子 #196 ---
Hi Dale

I do not consider signals and market as two different things, so generally formation of a fractal is always forming one or more Balance Line signals.

I'll try to explain - let's suppose that:market is in up trend price is above Allegator's lines and 1st fractal has been formed.

Forming the fractal itself means that there is a retrace down at least 2 consecutive bars.

Until price is above the Alligator lines and there is no any other signals we consider that the move is up - so in general each of this 'at least 2 consecutive bars' has an balance line signal.

--- 帖子 #198 ---
No fractal cannot disapear once created. This means that you have at least 5 consecutive bars (may be more) and one of them has highest high or lowest low from the group. So until 5th bar is not compleated we cannot be sure that the fractal is valis.

Some softwares or scripts might show fractal on the 4th or event 3rd bar considering this as a help to their customers, but I dobt it is useful...

Metatrader is a great tool and I'm a big fan of it but ...

... if one does not have deep knowledge of the system, relying on some script to do the work, soon or later this behaviour will result significan loss.

I think that this system is so simple and natural that once known, trader does not need any tools to use it but the price...

--- 帖子 #207 ---
Hi Dale

Here I quote the "New Trading Dimentions" book because I like its simple and clear definitons.

"A buy signal is created when there are two consecutive histogram bars with higher highs than the most recent lowest low (a down peak).

...

A second buy signal cannot be created until the histogram moves at least one bar lower, creating a red bar. A new buy signal can then be created after two higher (green) bars."

I think this will help you more that my explanations...

Hi - how are you doing?

I was just playing around with it yesterday and it could be a 'scalpers' dream (at last on the DAX).

Yesterday I made $605.50 clear just out of the 'scalps' - this is not how I trade normally but I was getting bored and the DAX started moving around like crazy.  I don't recommend doing this unless you are working with a very high volatility instrument and are prepared to take many (small) losses until you are up (once a position has turned into profit make sure that you move your stop OR use a trailing stop).  You also need to find an instrument that is in a strong trend and basically you use the system to buy the 'dips' i.e. you only open positions in the direction of the trend and take profit when they turn into profit.  Then - wait again until the price is going against the trend then buy the dip again.  In other words - let's say the trend is up - when you get a valid fractal sell signal you place a buy limit order one tick below the fractal NOT a sell stop as you normally would.  Get the picture?  Speed of order execution is important so that depends on your broker (and admittedly the broker where I trade the DAX is not particularly fast so if you have a 'fast' broker you should do well).  This is also not a system for newbies (actually I'm not sure it's a system at all).  The reason I say this is that in order for this to be profitable you have to concentrate and can't make a trade and then walk away - you have to drive it otherwise you'll run into problems.  Also - you need to be EXTREMELY fast and very familiar with your trading platform.  As a matter of fact if you do decide to try this you'd be amazed how well the Profitunity System hold together - I mean - if you follow it EXACTLY as you would have on the time frames for which it was intended it's almost as if you are 'cramming' days into minutes.  Even the signals that you get from AO and AC are valid.  The only problem is when you are trying to place orders based on AO of AC - because it is happening so fast it is sometimes impossible to place a stop order one tick above or below the signal bar because the price has more often than not moved past the high or low of the bar by the time you have even entered your order but then you just stay out.

Even although I have tried this and made a few $$$ I DO NOT ADVOCATE USING IT - the Profitunity System is, in my opinion, one of the best and reliable system and to muck around with it the way I have is not the right thing to do (I know that is contradictory to everything I have said above but I don't think that those kind of profits are sustainable).  I just thought that it was interesting to see how well the indicators work on this time frame.

--- 帖子 #241 ---
OK Dale I'll try to answer 2nd post 1st.

First of all we have to keep in mind that this is a trend system. That means that it is not designed for range trades, i.e. when bars are inside or close around the Alligator.

On the other hand don't take literaly "... put a stop order one tick abobe/below the bar's high/low..." - this push you into situation you;ve described - loosing - especially where price is close aroung lines.

This is not a scalping system - that means you cannot use all the time tight stops because they are aften hit by the volatility.

The question "Where to place stops?" though important, does not have a simple answer - depends on your account, style of trading, pain of loosing, etc.

--- 帖子 #242 ---
Hi folks,

For what it's worth - a word:

There seems to be a HUGE difference between the original Profitunity (Chaos) Trading System and the one contained in the second edition of the book. Having only covered the first two or three chapters relating to the system in the past hour or so it is very clear that the original system used the fractals as entry points whereas the system detailed in the second edition of the book uses bullish/bearish divergent bars for entry signals.

Why this makes such a difference is if you read back on my earlier posts today I was finding two things happening:

1 - Once my buy or stop orders were hit the price would almost immediately retrace (which logically, now that I think about it, is quite correct because the fractals actually represent points of resistance so if your order is hit just a few points or pips too early you are actually buying or selling at a point of resistance).

2 - I was also very concerned about the fact that it would appear that a lot of the time you would be missing out on huge rallys.

Basically, the way I read it, in the second edition the fractals are used to add to positions already opened and not for initial entry.

isto: Comments on this?

Also - there is nothing mentioned in the book about what happens in the following case:

A bearish divergent bar appears

You place a sell stop one (or a few ticks) below the low of the bar

The sell stop gets triggered

You place a stop loss one (or a few ticks) above the signal bar

You place a buy stop order one (or a few ticks) above the signal bar (same price as the stop loss)

So far - so good

The market goes down in your favour (making a small profit)

The next bar opens and the market starts going against you

Your stop loss and buy stop detailed above get triggered (now a loss on the above position) (by this time a buy fractal has appeared and has just been triggered as well)
Where do you place the stop loss for this newly opened position?

It would appear that in a trending market this works fantastically BUT in a range bound market this thing will finish you off.

BUT, having said that, I am following the system to the letter as detailed in the book and the book specifically says that it should work in any market, any timeframe, and any instrument!

How do YOU determine whether the market is trending or range bound?

Also - it is designed to take things like commentary and market sentiment out of the equation i.e. mechanical trading.

What seems to be becoming clear (unless you can throw some more light on the subject) that this system will set you up to take small loss after small loss after small loss UNTIL a trend starts to develop and you just have to hope that the ensuing trend makes up for all of these small losses when it comes. Would that be a reasonable assumption?

I have tried to contract the Profitunity Website for traders of this system but they are closed (should open today though).

Any ideas or thoughts?

Regards,

Dale.

Hi Dale

Hard questions you're asking... :surprised

Let's try:

Unfortunately there is no answer like "Put your stop loss here."

Generally there are 3 hard to decide delemas on tradewhen to enter when/where to stop when/where to take profit

Answers of these question depends: on market; on pair; on broker; on your account; on your trading style... Everyone could continue this list.

Let's try a sample - one of the brokers I use has 1 pip spread for EURUSD and 15 for GBPCAD. It is obvious that I cannot use the same distance stop-loss on both, can I?

Another broker has 3 pips spread generaly but during news time spread becomes 25 pips sometimes, so choosing a stop loss here will depend not on pair but on time.

Other situations also exists, but I hope you've got the point

I do not see a reason to avoid a new entry as a workaround ...

If you think about you'll agree that it is not possible to cover all situations that live trade offers.

This is only the system. As anything else in the world it has good and bad part.

This best advantage of this particular system is that it is clear and clarifies what happens on the market not caring why this happens... It is just a style of trade and Bill is kind enough to share it with us.

Somewhere is his books he said:

... each trader trades his own believes ...[and] ... this is why even if one is trading side by side the very same method with very same rules the result will differ.

I quote this by hart and the words might be different but you get the point, don't you?

Yes this is right in the center of 10! This is why he has written Trading Chaos 2nd Edition offering Divergetn Bar as alternative tool for ranging market.

I personally use Alligato and Gator (available in MT4)

I do not believe in mechanical trading - market is live thanks to the traders - if mechanical trading is at all possible that meand that exchanges will become a large robot factory and profit will disapear...

There is no one single trader without a loss. You'll face losses, small or large. It doesn't matter how many they are - important is to keep them smaller than your profit - obvious, isn't it?

There was a strong move down earlier today which closed below a previously invalid fractal point.  It was invalid, at first, because prices were still above the alligator's teeth (the red line).  It became valid, however, because at the time the price fell to hit the fractal point, price was below the red line.

I waited for a close below the fractal.  I know that the Profitunity books all talk about putting orders "one tick below", but I have seen prices go and hit that one tick below only to go the other direction.  Waiting for a close below the fractal point is a lot safer in my book.

My next order is waiting just below the bar I entered on because, in addition to hitting the sell fractal, it was also a "Red Zone" signal with both the AO and the AC the same color.

We'll see how this shapes up.  It looks good, though.  I'm worried about NFP tomorrow, though.  As long as it is good news for the USD I should be okay.

--- 帖子 #272 ---
Actually, that's a good question. If I am waiting for a close below a fractal point, I will usually make a point to be watching the market at the time the candle completes. If it completes beneath the fractal, or if I can tell several minutes before the bar completes that it WILL close beneath the fractal, then I just place a market order.

Sometimes you can't be there, so I will place either buy or sell stops, but I usually prefer to be there when the candle updates. I don't trade anything less than the 4 hr chart, though so, even on days when I am working, at the most I only miss two candle updates a day.

As an update to the GBP/USD trade I entered into yesterday, as you can see from the attached chart, through the London session, last night, price had been slowly working its way down. Then, when NFP came out better than expected, price started to really move down. Needless to say I was quite happy about that. But, as soon as it started down it began retracing. Thankfully it didn't retrace too far, though. The end result is that it sort of went nowhere.

Looking at where it ended up for the week, price is below the alligator, so the tone is bearish: take all sell signals and ignore bull signals (except for the bullish divergent bar!?). AO is still moving down and is actually negative. AC, on the other hand, is negative but accelerating up.

In the end, I hope that this is just the market breathing a little: after the big move down on Thursday, and NFP, the GBP just needs to gather its strength before continuing to fall. We'll just have to see what next week brings.

--- 帖子 #294 ---
Hi Tommy,

Sure , You can use this indicator, I had written this indicator to help me to identify the zones.

This indicator is written in Metastock formula language. So it will work in Metastock. But with small changes it should work in other charting software also.

If you are using Metastock then I can upload this indicator for you or you can copy/paste the following code in indicator builder.

This indicator consists of three parts

Zone_Green

If(Fml( "Profitunity - PTG AC Green") AND Fml( "Profitunity - PTG AO Green"),1,0)

Zone_Red

If(Fml( "Profitunity - PTG AC Red") AND Fml( "Profitunity - PTG AO Red"),1,0)

Zone_Grey

If((Fml( "Profitunity - PTG AC Green") AND Fml( "Profitunity - PTG AO RED") ) OR (Fml( "Profitunity - PTG AC RED") AND Fml( "Profitunity - PTG AO Green") ),1,0)

Hope this will help you.

regards

tej

--- 帖子 #297 ---
Isto,

I just reread New Trading Dimensions a few weeks ago, and I am pretty sure that, with respect to zone trades, the book says that you buy on the close of green AO and green AC as long as the bar has a higher close than the bar before it.  So, if a green/green situation comes up, but the candle has a lower close than the candle before it, it would not be taken.  But, if green/green happened on the next bar, and that bar had a higher close, then you would buy on the close at that point.

At least I think that's what the book says... I could be wrong.

--- 帖子 #300 ---
The concept of the bullish/bearish divergent bar is a tough one to grasp.  It took me quite a while, too.  When looking at the chart you posted, the last white bar would NOT be a bullish divergent bar.  True, it is away from the alligator's mouth; true, there is angulation with the blue line (alligator's jaw); but in order to be a bullish divergent bar, it has to make a new low and also close in the upper half of the bar.  That particular bar, while it did close in the top half of the bar, did not make a lower low than the bar before it.

It takes some practice, but after a little while the bullish/bearish divergent bars will, literally, jump right off the page at you.

Good luck.

Well Protei,

I doubt anybody could answer your questions. Bill Williams few times underlined in his books that "every trader trades his own believs".

On the same chart two traders see two different lanscapes and got different signals.

I mentioned mine: For me basic is the trend because this is a trend method. So first we have to have trend; then we have to have fractal and when it is break in trend direction we enter.

Yes, you could miss some move, yes it might be too late, but think about which is first: to enter the trade to win the trade

It doesn't matter for me whether there is move or not. I cannot guess where the price will be, or how long it will move, or whatever else concirning the future.

I can only consider the signals that are already on the chart and to decide: Are they enough for me to enter, what is the risk, is it acceptable for me.

If I answer yes I put stop order. If not - look around for the next move...

Hi tej

3AO are 3 green acceleration bars below zero on a down trend, or

3 red acceleration bars above zero on a up trend.

This is a signal that trend is slowing and might turn around so it is used to enter in the opposite direction...

I would like to share my viewpoint. Whenever I have faced such difficult situation. I try to resolve it with the help of Rules of the System.

And if i still have any doubt. I prefer to resolve it with Risk / Reward ratio

I believe in any trade our potential Reward should be at least 2 time the risk we are taking.  [ Bcoz our Main Aim is to Make Money ]

In the above case, I can think of following 4 scenario's

i) There has been a vertical rally... mkt may undergo some correction may be upto 23.6% or 38.2% fib ratio. Since we are getting an

entry near the top.... our risk/reward ratio should be better than 1:2

ii) This might the begining of a new down trend.... [ V could hope for  bigger profits ]

iii) Market might just be taking rest and it may remain sideways and resume it's journey upward, then we will get an entry on the break of bullish fractal.

iv) Worst possible case.... mkt may hit both the triggers, first down, then up

and finally go down...

So, I would prefer to go short...... bcoz risk/reward is favourable....

This is my personal view.... You can correct me wherever I am wrong..

Hi tej

I'll try to answer your questions

learnign is one of the action that I admire very much

As to comments - everybody is free to comment whichever aspect of the thread (I prefer positive though )

I think that Risk / Reword could be considered after the trade is closed. Trying to calculate any ratio during the trade, or even before to enter it is waste of time (this is my point of view).

Because it you do, this means that you can predict what the market will do, where will go, how long will move. If you can - you do not need any system. If you cannot - this is loss of time.

Shure the main purpose is to make money... These are rules for - we are blind for the future (at least some of us ) - so rules tell us:

if this and this happen (rule), act so and so (obey the rules)

Rules are created (usually) after long observation and reflect some repleating behaviour of the price under definite conditions.

But when market is bored it changes this repleating behaviour and this is why it does not work 100% of the time. (let's say some news is comming on)

Then traders have to face some losses...

The last sentance is totally wrong! (sorry)

I prefer to get profit without risk at all or without trading at all

But this is not up to our preferences...

Here the preferences are issued and done my the market.

We have two choices:be prepared whatever market decides don't be prepared (act under personal preferences)

If we act according our preferences and do not care about market's guess who will be the winner and who the looser?

you've listed some opportunities (correct or wrong, it doesn't matter here, now). Be prepared for each of them. This way your chances (to win oe lose) increase from one to four (as you've listed them).

Sorry for the long post, I believe all these are important...

--- 帖子 #380 ---
Well as promised (to isto) here is what I have found works for me:

I have found that working on the 15 minute and longer timeframes using ONLY AO and AC I am making far more consistent profits than I ever have using the system as a whole as detailed in Trading Chaos Second Edition.

I find that identifying the divergent bars is a very subjective thing i.e. is there an angle between the divergent bar and the Alligators teeth / jaw? Is there enough angulation? I'm never sure.

Anyway - according to the book - the AO is the best indicator around and, although it is NOT recommended by Bill and Justine Williams to use this indicator on its own, they also say that using this indicator correctly 'should be worth at least seven figures to you in the next few years'.

I think the reason for making the divergent bars the first entry point is to get you into the trend reversal early to maximize profits. My problem is that I don't really care whether the profits are maximized - just as long as I am making consistent profits - and this seems to be working nicely for me.

All I am doing is trading the Dow, S&P, Nasdaq, and DAX using AO and AC (the 15 minute charts seem to be the best for me because I am one of those traders that needs to be trading all day every day otherwise I don't feel like I have a job). Basically - I have the AO and AC open on my chart - and place a market order to buy the moment the new bar changes from red to green and place a market order to sell the moment the new bar changes from green to red. I hold on to the positions - no matter what - until the very first 'contradictory' bar changes color on the AC. That's it.

The trick to this is that on the shorter time frames I have found that both Metatrader and my other brokers' trading platform may present the wrong color AO and AC bars the instant that the new bar appears (I think it has to do with the immediate opening price). The way I get around this is I wait for the new bar to appear and then just hit 'refresh' a couple of time until I am sure that the bar is not going to change color and then, depending on the 'constant' color, I open my position (this is tied to a previous problem that I described where fractals 'disappear' i.e. the platforms draw the fractal BEFORE the second bar to the right of the fractal bar has closed and if the price then goes in the same direction of the fractal at any point while drawing the third bar the fractal disappears).

Also - I wait until there is a nice 'high' or 'low' saucer formed before opening a position i.e. sometimes the saucer (or oscillator) is just above or below the zero or middle line - I stay away from those. I know the height of the saucer or oscillator is purely dependent on price BUT the way I interpret things - the 'higher' or 'lower' the top of the saucer or oscillator - the greater the 'conviction' of the traders and the stronger the movement will be in the opposite direction.

My main problem with the entire system as detailed in the second edition of the book is the fact that EVERY SINGLE TIME a fractal signal is taken there is an immediate retractment. I contacted Justine Williams about this and she said to place your stop orders a little further away from the fractal to avoid the order getting 'falsely' executed but I started to find that no matter HOW far away from the fractal I placed an order it somehow ALWAYS got executed and then the price would retract. I tried everything - including placing a buy stop order below a fractal when the system was telling me that I should be placing a sell stop order etc. etc. but most times I was wrong and then lost money by getting stopped out. I also tried using fibo and pivot points - just to 'unsure' for me.

Anyway - look here:

--- 帖子 #382 ---
Gladly - except that I will only start doing it from the end of next week.

The reason being is that starting this week (Monday) I have drawn up a spreadsheet to make weekly targets for myself (the main reason being is that over the past couple of months I have messed up badly simply because I have held on to profitable positions that have invariably turned into losses simply because of greed and not knowing when to stop). My target basically from now on is 20% per week of my capital. If I hit that in an hour on Monday morning - I'm gone for the week. If I don't - as long as by Friday I have made my target - things are good. This idea FORCES me to take profit when a position reaches 20% of its cost (or to at least place a stop loss at that point assuming I am further into a profit situation).

Money management (in my opinion) is the 'make or break' of any system. Taking profit on trades (BEFORE they eventually turned into losses) and subtracting bad trades (those that never turned to a profit) for the past six months - I could be a wealthy man right now!!! I'm not - and this is the main reason. Food for thought!

You would be surprised at how compounding your profits builds up - just try it. Don't aim for that 'sparkling' trade - plod along - you'll do well.

Anyway - good trading!

Edit:

Oh - and by the way - using AO and AC as desribed above - make sure that AC is also 'high' or 'low' before opening a position. The reason I say this is because when it is hanging around the middle or zero line - there is no 'conviction' in the market - and you will find that this is where the brokers are just hanging around trying to catch stops (it just happened to me while I was typing this message - because - I was not concentrating)!!!

Second edit:

There is one other 'magic bullet' that I forgot to put in my first message.  I have Stochastics (14/3/3) open on my chart as well.  Although this is not pure Bill Williams it gives me a sense of 'comfort' i.e. I will only sell when Stochs are above 80, AO is green, and AC is red and only buy when stochs are below 20, AO is red, and AC is green.  I am experimenting with the idea of 'hedging' positions when I get valid AO and AC signals but Stochs are around the 50 line and flat.

Regards,

Dale.

--- 帖子 #395 ---
Hello tej

Here is I think a classic sample of dbar (beginning is in post #388).

DBar has two major properties to qualify as DBar. it is far away from the red line there is acute angle between price and red line

There are valid and not valid DBars, visible on the chart below.

1st bunch of DBars (not valid) do not interrupt the trend and down move continue.

2nd DBar (valid) result into a sideway move (down trend is interupted at the moment).

Gerenaly speaking sideway is the place where trend might:continue previous move reverse So here DBar gives us just a signal that a reverse might happen.

There is no rule that DBar will cause trend reverse. It is a signal the trend might reverse in near future.

A Signal appearace does not mean that we must act immediately (place order).

A Signal appearace just says "be careful. an possible event in front."

That's all

And trader acts according the rules he/she follows and according the believes he/she has about the chart landscape.

Hope this will clear a little bit the matter

--- 帖子 #401 ---
I wish very much to be able to answer this question

If I knew I would screw down the market in few weeks

Well, back to the question:

AO = Momentum

AC = Acceleration

So when we have red AC and green AO this means that general tendency is price to go up while the speed of the move is slowing (the moving power has less steam to continue).

Red AC also means that slowing down acceleration is facing some strong resistance and if thie resistance is stronger than general move (AO) it could reverse the move and Acceleration will speed up in the opposite direction (down) trailing behing the Momentum

4th entry - AO zero line cross down - adding order

end finally - after gap fills - exit

--- 帖子 #466 ---
The only signal the I know works 100% from this system is the first signal. Which is the counter trend trade, they call is wiseman1, I call it the rubber band effect.

Looking at eurusd right now, the price has left the alligator in 1 swift move down, and if you imagine a rubber band around the alligator and the price, the move your stretch the rubber the more chances or the rubbe band snapping back. In other words if price goes up in 1 big swift move I usually wait for the next candle and I sell, for a small profit, my target is usually the alligator for exit. same if the price moves down in 1 swift move, I buy at next candle and exit when price reaches alligator again.

This is the only signal that works all the time in forex and it works in any time frame. All other signals are trend following signals.

just my 2 pips.

--- 帖子 #476 ---
Well Protei, You have to bear in mind that not each Bbar is a valid one.

Two main conditions have to be met so as to qualify a bar as DBar: In a strong trend to have price moved far away from Alligator's line to have acutre angel with Alligator's line

on the chart of the post above you have neither of these...

Acctually I see a ranging stock raghly between 29 - 31 levels. Look how many bars you have in there - almost whole chart...

This is why once hit DBar reverse and hit stoploss.

It is wrong to trade trend system on a range market!

Hi Protei,

I have been thinking about this from quite sometime.

In the book : New Trading Dimensions. Williams Says :

These two sentences tell us what to expect,

Since we are following a trend following System. It will make money only 15 to 30% of the time (i.e. when the market is in Trend)

Now, this seems a very pessimistic statement. But Truth is always hard to digest.

So we could do two things....

i) Keep searching the markets and trade only those markets which giving us clear trend

ii) Or may be drop down to lower time frames & take a trade when we see a clear cut trend in lower time frame. { If mkt is sideways in daily time frame, we could drop down to hourly, If hrly is also sideways then maybe 30 min, 15 min or even 5 min) But the problem with lower time frames is, we will have to be very quick and profits will be smaller.

--- 帖子 #538 ---
this a reply to post #537

Well, this system is not perfect one. It (as any other system) generate losses.

Here the most importent becomes trader decisions and trader overview about current state of the market...

As for the rules, you might motice that system from New Trading Dimentions is altered a lot in Trading Chaos 2nd edition...

Usual explanation is that on time the system has been created, trends have been longer than nowadays. These longer trends are replaced with choppy markets and higher volotility.

Perhaps this is why DBar has been announced...

When I've started trading this system, I've used it as a Holy Grail, i.e. signal = order.

Now, I believe that this is more an attempt to explain how (and why) market behaves.

When one knows what and why is happening, exact rules are no more necessary.

It doesn't matter whether order will be opened 1 or 10 tick(s) above the break, because trader's goal is to catch the big move...

Hi,

Have some of you tried to modify the way to exit when a fractal breakout is not working so good?

I think the idea of the breakout is really good. Bill Williams wrote that, if we are not in the market, it is better to wait for the alligator to sleep and place a stop order for both last valid up and last valid down fractal.

I think that if a fractal breakout occurs and this breakout is a valid one, the the price should have a strong move and it should not go back under the fractal. That's a bit like if you have a trading market moving between a support level and a resistance level, then if it breaks out in one direction, if the price comes back again inside the channel, it is likely to be a false breakout. Also the bar which is doing the breakout is as much important than the fractal bar.

As we want to enter as soon as the fractal is broken to get the most of the move, then we have to change the way to exit. What do you think of using something like the following:

When the breakout occurs, we wait for the bar to close and we put a stoploss order 1 tick below or above the bar. But we don't wait for that next bar to close, as soon as the stoploss is triggered we exit.

Well I'm only trying to find a good way to reduce losses and I'm really insterested if you're experimenting a bit on a way to reduce losses and you want to share with us.

Cheers,

Daniel

Great thread.  I used the Bill Williams methods for about a year with good success.  It's all about the add-on trades.  I ditched the oscillators and now only use the fractals as entries, add-ons, and support/resistence.  I just couldn't keep up with all of the oscillator signals.  I occasionally use the alligator to add on, gauge runaway markets, and when to start looking to get out when price is in the mouth.

Even though I'm doing completely different stuff now, the lessons learned were huge.  It's all about piling it on when you catch the trend.  Up until I saw this thread I haven't seen too many people do well with the system.  Mainly because they were afraid to add on.  You'll get eaten alive trying to catch breakouts out of the alligator in the forex market without taking the add on signals to make up the difference.

--- 帖子 #598 ---
Ajone92:

I have traded all or part of the Profitunity way since 1999--futures initially, Forex since early 2004. In my experience, the Profitunity way can be profitable in all time frames and in all markets just as Williams claims for it; but it has been the most successful for me when I took my action reads off of the daily time frame charts.

As for divergent price bars, I have not found any reasonablly consistent signficance to a divergent bar that did not appear after a heathy Alligator chase.

Protei:

I too often trade a system that is not textbook Profitunity, but I would argue that it needs no help to be a profitable system. I emblish it because I believe my tweaks increases the probability of a trade being profitable.

Williams says in all three of his books that the Elliott Wave is the underlying structure of a market, and that fractals are the underlying structure of Elliott Waves. Williams says in New Trading Dimensions (p.62), "If the current price is outside the Alligator's mouth, we are in an impulsive wave of one degree or another. If the price is meandering around the Balance lines, we are in a reactive wave of one degree or another." We know that ideally, we want to enter our trade early in an impulsive EW, and that we do not want to enter our trade while it is in a reactive EW. Williams says in Trading Chaos 2nd Edition (p.142), " A Fractal is always a change in behavior caused by new incoming information (chaos)." Putting all this together means we can indeed trade the EW without counting waves. For my own trading, I use these realities of market behavior to decide whether or not I want to take the 2nd Wise Man signal (Super AO signal)... I will even occassionally buy off a fractal low when it is in an impulsive EW or sell off a fractal high that is in an impulsive EW.

Profitunity is certainly not the only system that can be traded profitably; in fact, it may not even be the best system one might choose, but it is a darn good one built on a uniquely solid technical foundation; and it has been a good one for me.

...\larry.bye

--- 帖子 #613 ---
Food for Thought:Before Trading Chaos II, we were taught to look for a quiet Alligator--extended balance lines relatively flat (the flatter the better)--and AO and AC values on or near their zero lines.  This setup was designed to catch fractal breakouts.  We judged the quality of that setup signal by how long a market looked like this.  We usually got whipsawed more than we wanted, but it was in what Williams called "the low rent district" (small losses). Trading Chaos II teaches a significantly different setup.  We are now looking for a major bottom or top--the Alligator is in full pursuit of bulls or bears, AO and probably AC are supporting the Alligator's direction, and a new extreme price candle is divergent with a strong angleulation.  This setup is designed to catch key reversals in a market. Remember, the 3 Wise Men strategy gets us into a countertrend trade.  It is essential that there be a high probability of a market reversal.  You may want to use additional indicators that the current trend direction is exhausted.  For my own Profitunity trading, I require that the new low be lower than the two previous fractal lows, and that the new high be higher than the two previous fractal highs.  In addition, I usually will require that the current trend extreme be at least a 62% retracement of the previous swing in the opposite direction (I am more comfortable when the retracement exceeds 76.4%). ...\larry.bye

All your winners are full loads!

--- 帖子 #708 ---
I read Williams' book and I was quite dissapointed. I see that many people follow his 'chaos' approach, but this is how I see it. I don't like to be destructive, but I like to call things by their names. On the other hand, some contributions are quite valuable, as I depict below.

In addition this is my opinion. If there is something wrong below, please do not hesitate to respond this post. If I am wrong, I prefer to know.

Fractals: local maximums and minimums. Nothing else.

Awesome Oscillator: the difference between the 34-period and 5-period simple moving averages of the bar's midpoints (H+L)/2. That is, the MACD of 5 and 34 applied to the midpoint of High and Low instead tothe close.

Acceleration Oscillator:
MIDPOINT PRICE = ( HIGH + LOW ) / 2

AO = SMA ( MIDPOINT PRICE, 5 ) – SMA ( MIDPOINT PRICE, 34 )

AC = AO – SMA ( AO, 5 )

That is, the Acceleration Oscillator is the MACD histogram, i.e., the MACD minus its signal. Again, the MACD computed on hte midpoint. Nothing new. (well, the MACD signal is usually an EMA, not a SMA)

The Alligator: another way of displaying three moving averages.

The interesting contributions I see here are:

- all the signals of buy and sell described for the AO. Deep study, which at least at first glance, is valid also for MACD.

- the Alligator, it is not the use fo a smoothed MA but the forward displacement what makes it extremely interesting.

- the Gator Oscillator, which depicts two MACDs in the same graphic (one for the jaw/teeth MA and one for the teeth/lips). I think this oscillator deserves more in-depth study, which I will try to do in my free time.

Best regards and lots of pips to everyone.

gonso

Gonso, I like to call things by their name as well: You`ve read the books (Chaos2 as well?) - but you haven`t digested them yet.

You have seen the tires, a little engine, some spoilers.... but you haven`t recognized the BMW yet - nor the instructions how to race!!!!! This is understandable, as BW is a top systems creator, but a lousy writer.

BW has taken parts of TA, reshaped, retooled and renamed them - and put them in a connection (for example alligator as deciding when and how to use fracal) and finally applied a unique mm system to all of this.

Does his system work on cable all the time? No. Does it work on currencies all the time? YES. Because it will tell  you which underlying NOT to touch at a given time.

So read the book(s) 3-5 times - just to memorize the facts. Only then try to analyze the parts and their interaction. And finally the mm.

BW system is a self-contained closed system, nothing should be taken away, adding won`t help much either - just like P&F, 3LB, Ichimoku, M.I.D.A.S. ....just to name a few.

--- 帖子 #738 ---
It can be used on any time frame but the method is designed to catch long trends.  Since trading Forex for the last 18 months I struggled to find the appropriate time frame to achieve the most pips.  I wanted to be able to profit in the London market while I was sleeping (I live in California).  Dr. Bill Williams lives close to me and he has become a friend, and he invited me over a couple of times to his home for some private consulting.  He suggested I play longer time frames.  He said to stay away from day trading because I would never achieve the large gains he is used to achieving.

I played around with 1 hr, 2 hr, 4 hr time frames and finally came to the conclusion that 2hr time frames were optimal in trading the Forex for me.  I trade a dozen different pairs but I like the EUR/JPY and the GBP/JPY the best because of their large pip movements.  With the 2 hr time frames I can easily count the waves and it is most dependable.  I also look at 4 hr time frames and sometimes daily's to confirm an entry.  I use a lot of BDB's to enter a trade.  I guess about 50/50 between BDB's and fractals to enter trades.  I also use 15 min time frames to confirm a BDB on a 2 hr time frame to enter.  Many times a full 5 waves occur on a 15 min time frame and the first 15 min fractal break occurs on a BDB 2 hr time frame which only gives me additional confirmation of a good calculated trade.  Once I enter I add on according to what the 2 hr time frame tells me to do.

Although at times I do trade 5 min and  15 time frames I do not rely on only trading within those time frames.  Over the long haul I usually end up only breaking even and the stress of those time frames can wear you out.  I would rather just wait for a good 2 hr time frame set up.  I do use those lower time frames to exit trades, especially the 15 min time frames as the Forex can radically move over 2 hrs as I'm sure you know, and I would rather cash out and then re-enter to continue the 2 hr time frame trend.

Hope this helps........

--- 帖子 #764 ---
The best way to gain a sense of what an author is trying to convey is to probably read the book. This is a great book. But how amazing is it that two people can read the same book but come away with completely different interpretations?

I didn't see any system described in Bill Williams book. Sure he talks about waves and gets into specifics and talks about certain indicator settings and so on. But, I mean if you read the book and possess a decent sense of reading comprehension how can you say there is a system here?

On page 2 it says, "Nonsense replaced common sense. Our interest became centered around moving averages, stochastics, RSI, MACD, ...Market profile hit the scene but was hampered because it used parametric statistics in a nonparametric world(the market)...we have taken a practical and commonsense job of trading, dressed it in fancy language, and turned it into something very abstract and difficult...the process of trading has been transformed into a pseudo-intellectual science; traders think they must strain their brains at it in order to profit...good trading does not emanate from the head, it emanates from the gut and the heart"

I'll leave it at that. It just amazes me how people actually focus on everything BUT trading. The project targets into an unknowable future, they backtest and look for nonexistent patterns, they misinterpret texts....they do everything except pay attention to getting a good sense of what is happening at the right edge of the chart.

--- 帖子 #765 ---
I am gradually working my way towards more naked trading but I do like some indicators that I find help a lot.

One is the RSI - but I use a RSI 3.  I have become very used to how it signals, but only on a daily time frame.  (Sometimes on the four hour, below that is gets wonky.)  I set it with 20 and 80 and find that the nice tight M and W divergence patters it makes at tops and bottom are really good.  It is also good to draw trend lines on and watch to see where they break.  There are other signals that it generates but that is a whole separate topic.

Another is the Directional Index system that I set at a standard 14 with horizontal lines at 16 and 40.  Signals tend to be valid above 16 and tend to end as the ADX turns down and crosses back below 40.

Combining these with fractals and the AO are really good in my opinion.

Two others I use are right in the chart, the BW Zone indicator turns the bars green, red, or grey depending on the AO and AC being in phase.  Another is one that tries to alert you to the BDB.  Emphasis on tries , but it does give you a heads up and then the RSI 3 is a good filter.

And of course fractals.  Got have them on the chart.

Might as well add Bollinger Bands for some more information.

Then there are trend lines, Fibonacci levels and so on.

Finally I have a bar timer that tells you how much of the bar remains before a new bar occurs.  Not really needed in daily trading.

Here is a sample with some signals on the RSI 3 shown.

I find it all helps me to know the market's structure and I get to see the indicators behaving as I expect they should if I understand the structure correctly.

http://www.elkvalleygold.com/Forex/F...%20dec3109.jpg

The above GBPUSD chart is at a point where I suspect it will rally up in to a wave Three. I have been scalping it a bit until it reaches a smaller wave 2 then I will try for a long BW daily trade so that I can catch the Three and ride it.

--- 帖子 #768 ---
Dr. Bill Williams definitely has a "method" but not a system.  There is quite a distinction in that.

What he is trying to communicate is that market patterns cannot perfectly duplicated so it's futile to expect markets to repeat the same patterns over and over again with the same price action.

He method is based off of trader's behavior not price itself. His indicators are set up to take advantage of market or trader "behavior".  That is what BDB's and fractals are about.  His entry signals are specific based off BDB's, fractals, and what the moving averages or "Alligator" is doing at that specific time.

Exits are based off the same thing.  What each bar is doing in relation to the Alligator.  He states that his "method" is the "Holy Grail" of trading which I would have to agree considering how well his method gets you into and out of a trade.

When you truly understand his method you'll be hard pressed to come across a better one and if you do I sure would like to see it.  I have done many trades where I caught the top of a trend and exited and the bottom of the trend.  I have done it in many different time frames but for the Forex I mainly trade off of 2 hour time frames and at times 15 min tf's.

--- 帖子 #769 ---
Well, those things can help give you an idea of what's happening, sure. But after a while you really don't need them. You don't need all of that methodological complexity to understand tops and bottoms and middles - just a good understanding of proportion and of highs and lows.

Well anyway, he does describe the process of going from a novice to a successful trader. I believe he describes being in the most proficient state as being able to flow deeply within chaos, or something to that effect. I don't have the book handy. But, in my opinion, the methods described are really meant as helpers and as training wheels, until you know exactly what to look for, and how to approach trading.

So, while he does include a very detailed explanation of "method", there is one sentence in the book towards the back that reads "90% of what we hear is lies". I think that might be appropo. But certainly, if one is more comfortable with exact wave counts and fractals and the 5/34 MACD, then great.

--- 帖子 #812 ---
I've been trading using his Trading Chaos second edition book.  (I've been trading with the first edition system, which is GREAT!) and I have to say I am SORELY disappointed in the "Wise Men" and the new oscillators.  But my main beef is with what is arguably the cornerstone of the new system, that which decides the bulk of your entries. The first "wise man", the Bullish Divergence Bar.

I would seriously warn people against trading the bullish divergence bar.  Using the Alligator and good angulation doesn't seem to help in the slightest; for every cherry picked trade you win, you get stopped out (with big SLs even H1 and H4) five to ten times.  I've practiced using this tech on H1, H4, and 15M Tfs.   In my final analysis the BDB is a dangerous counter trend technique, and is quite hazardous to the health of any account using it.  Frankly it is not working live at all thus far for me.  Whereas Trading Chaos first edition does work, often and well.

If you really must pick tops and bottoms; pin bars on the H1 and H4 are a MUCH safer tried and true method, pin bars with pivots and fibs being even more profitable.   In fact the only time the bullish divergence bar has worked for me has been in the presence of a good pin bar.  The problem with the BDB is that with angulation you end up placing your stop well before a pin bar forms.  And then even if it does, you usually hadn't gained anymore profit than if you had waited for a pin bar to form and close and then price action.

Basically angulation is just pin bar trading, but good angulation (by the rules of the system) forms often without pin bars and this is where trading it fails, might as well just trade the pins.

Where you lose big money is if you place your buy or sell stop a couple pips above or below the BDB, you frequently get your stop gently "tapped" by a pin and then the market can continue trending.  Conversly if you place your stops too far away from the BDB it is nearly impossible to break even, if the market continues trending.  And profits are generally lower IF the BDB is even true.

I am quite confused why Bill Williams shoehorned the BDB into his system and turned his system indicators that were built around trading with the trend, into indicators to trade against it.  The exact process of picking out a BDB and putting a stop on it requires trading against an Alligator that is in the process of closing.  So really this technique works against the purpose of the Alligator as well.

I am in the process of back testing bullish div bars but as I am also taking price action based off the MFI into account this is taking me some time, finding a lot of losers so far though.

As for me, I am going to stick with my MFI, 5/34/5 MACD, Fractals, and EWs, using the Profitunity indicators as they were originally intended, as a trend spotting and trading system, not this ultra counter trend bottom and top picking stuff that does not pan out often enough to have profitable system expectancy.

Has anyone else had issues with this? Any tips? I'm seriously disappointed right now after being so excited over the "brand new indicators" and "revised system" a while ago when I pored over and digested Trading Chaos second edition.  This system just does not trade as well as its examples, even when you are being ultra conservative following the rules.

And don't even get me started about adding lots based on the AO.  Or the part in the book on page 126 where he suggests you could even in theory trade off the first signal bar from the AO and be highly profitable.  If you did, you'd wipe out an account in short order.  Don't believe me, back test it on any currency pair.  I'm starting to see why the second edition was 3/4ths filled with psychobabble.  The second edition system is weak sauce IMO.

Nevermind the AO, if you just traded squat to squat on the MFI you would be profitable, and wouldn't be getting big SL hits either.

But like I said, I didn't just post this only to vent my indignity at the second edition of Trading Chaos, but also to see if people who use the first edition system have actually incorporated the second well into their trading.  So please do, take my points and tell me if you agree or disagree with them.    I'm subbed to this thread and have seen good live trades using this system.  Apparently it is possible...
